class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drugs-acting-on-cardiovascular-system">DRUGS ACTING ON CARDIOVASCULAR SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-acting-on-cardiovascular-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>PAUL KWASI -RN</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-and-secondary-hypertension">Primary and Secondary Hypertension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-and-secondary-hypertension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypertension can either primary or secondary. No underlying cause can be identified</li>
<li>The actual level of pressure that can be considered hypertensive is difficult to define; it depends on a number of factors, including the patient's age, sex, race, and lifestyle.</li>
<li>As a working definition, many cardiovascular treatment centers consider that a diastolic pressure of 90 mm Hg or higher or a systolic pressure of 140 mm Hg or higher represents hypertension.</li>
<li>Hypertension is considered to be stage I, or mild, if diastolic pressure is 90 to 99 mm Hg and/or systolic pressure is 140 to 159 mm Hg. Stage II, or moderate, hypertension is diastolic pressure of 100 to 109 mm Hg and/or systolic pressure of 160 to 179 mm Hg. Stage III, or severe, hypertension exists when diastolic pressure is 110 mm Hg or greater and/or systolic pressure is 180 mm Hg or greater.</li>
</ul>
<p>There are three general approaches to the pharmacological treatment of primary hypertension.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The first involves the use of diuretics to reduce blood volume. The second employs drugs that interfere with the renin–angiotensin system, and the third is aimed at a drug-induced reduction in peripheral vascular resistance, cardiac output, or both.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A reduction in peripheral vascular resistance can be achieved directly by relaxing vascular smooth muscle with drugs known as vasodilators or indirectly by modifying the activity of the sympathetic nervous system.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>DIURETICS</p>
<p>• Diuretics are drugs that increase the rate of urine flow; clinically useful diuretics also increase the rate of excretion of sodium and accompanying anion chloride.</p>
<p>• Most clinical application of diuretics aim to reduce extracellular fluid volume by decreasing total sodium chloride volume.</p>
<p>• Diuretics alter excretion of sodium and also may modify handling of other cations(potassium, hydrogen and magnesium) anions (chloride, bicarbonate, hydrogen phosphate ), and uric acid</p>
<p>Clinical pharmacology of diuretics</p>
<p>• Edematous state :in heart failure, kidney disease and in renal failure.</p>
<p>• Non edematous state : in hypertension, nephrolithiasis hypercalcemia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-diuretics">classification of diuretics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>➢Loop diuretics : furosemide</p>
<p>➢Thiazide diuretics: hydrochlorothiazide</p>
<p>➢Potassium sparing diuretics: spironolactone</p>
<p>➢Osmotic diuretic: mannitol</p>
<p>➢Carbonic anhydrase inhibitors: acetazolamide (DIAMOX)</p>
<p>Hormones Acting on the Nephron / Diuretics and Their Site of Action</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-e058334e.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-high-ceiling-loop-diuretics">a)High Ceiling Loop Diuretics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-high-ceiling-loop-diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="furosemide-lasix">furosemide (Lasix)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#furosemide-lasix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Other Medications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ethacrynic acid (Edecrin)</li>
<li>Bumetanide (Bumex)</li>
<li>Torsemide (Demadex)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-pharmacological-action">Expected Pharmacological Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-pharmacological-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>High ceiling loop diuretics work in the ascending limb of loop of Henle to:</li>
<li>Block reabsorption of sodium and chloride and to prevent reabsorption of water, Cause extensive diuresis even with severe renal impairment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>High ceiling loop diuretics are used when there is an emergent need for rapid mobilization of fluid such as:</li>
<li>Pulmonary edema caused by heart failure</li>
<li>Conditions not responsive to other diuretics such as edema caused by liver, cardiac, or kidney disease; hypertension</li>
<li>These medications may also be used to treat hypercalcemia related to kidney stone formation.</li>
<li>Route of administration: Oral, IV, IM.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side effects</p>
<p>• Dehydration, hyponatremia, hypochloremia.</p>
<p>• Hypotension</p>
<p>• Ototoxicity (transient with furosemide and irreversible with ethacrynic acid)</p>
<p>• Hypokalemia (K+ less than 3.5 mEq/L</p>
<p>• Other adverse effects (hyperglycemia, hyperuricemia, and decrease in calcium and magnesium levels)</p>
<p>• Contraindications/Precautions ;Pregnancy Risk Category C , Avoid using these medications during pregnancy unless absolutely required. Use cautiously in clients who have diabetes and/or gout</p>
<p>Drug interaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Digoxin (Lanoxin) toxicity can occur in the presence of hypokalemia.</li>
<li>Concurrent use of antihypertensive can have additive hypotensive effect.</li>
<li>Hyponatremia can lead to decrease in lithium carbonate excretion, which may lead to toxicity.</li>
<li>NSAIDs reduce diuretic effect.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain the client’s baseline data to include orthostatic blood pressure, weight, electrolytes, and location and extent of edema.</li>
<li>Weigh clients at the same time each day; usually upon awakening.</li>
<li>Monitor the client’s blood pressure and input &amp; output.</li>
<li>Avoid administering the medication late in the day to prevent nocturia. Usual dosing time is 0800 and 1400.</li>
<li>Administer furosemide orally, IV bolus dose, or continuous IV infusion. Infuse IV doses at 20 mg/min or slower to avoid abrupt hypotension and hypovolemia.</li>
<li>If potassium level drops below 3.5 mEq/L, clients should be placed on a potassium supplement.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing administration cont.'</p>
<ul>
<li>If the medication is used for hypertension, teach clients to self-monitor blood pressure and weight by keeping a log.</li>
<li>Advise clients to get up slowly to minimize postural hypotension. If faintness or dizziness occurs, instruct clients to sit or lie down.</li>
<li>Teach clients to report significant weight loss, lightheadedness, dizziness, GI distress, and/ or general weakness to the provider.</li>
<li>Encourage clients to consume foods high in potassium, such as avocados and strawberries.</li>
<li>Instruct clients with diabetes to monitor for elevated blood glucose levels.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to observe for signs of low magnesium levels such as muscle twitching and tremors.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-thiazide-diuretics">b)Thiazide Diuretics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-thiazide-diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>hydrochlorothiazide (Hydrodiuril)</li>
</ul>
<p>Other Medications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chlorothiazide (Diuril)</li>
<li>Methyclothiazide (Enduron)</li>
</ul>
<p>Thiazide-type diuretics:</p>
<ul>
<li>indapamide (Lozide, Lozol)</li>
<li>chlorthalidone (Hygroton)</li>
<li>metolazone (Zaroxolyn)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action">Mechanism of action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-pharmacological-action">Expected Pharmacological Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-pharmacological-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Thiazide diuretics work in the early distal convoluted tubule to:</li>
<li>Block the reabsorption of sodium and chloride, and prevent the reabsorption of water at this site</li>
<li>Promote diuresis when renal function is not impaired</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Thiazide diuretics are often the medication of first choice for essential hypertension.</li>
<li>These medications may be used for edema of mild-to-moderate heart failure and liver and kidney disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<ul>
<li>dehydration</li>
<li>Hypokalemia (K+ less than 3.5 mEq/L)</li>
<li>Hyperglycemia</li>
</ul>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions</p>
<ul>
<li>Digoxin (Lanoxin) toxicity can occur in the presence of hypokalemia</li>
<li>Antihypertensive have additive hypotensive effects. Monitor the client’s blood pressure.</li>
<li>Hyponatremia can lead to decrease in lithium (Eskalith) excretion, which may lead to toxicity.</li>
<li>NSAIDs reduce diuretic effect</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Chlorothiazide may be administered orally and IV, all others can only be given orally.</li>
<li>Obtain the client’s baseline data to include orthostatic blood pressure, weight, electrolytes, and location and extent of edema.</li>
<li>Monitor the client’s potassium levels</li>
<li>Instruct clients to take the medication first thing in the morning; if twice-a-day dosing is prescribed, be sure the second dose is taken by 1400 to prevent nocturia.</li>
<li>Encourage clients to consume foods high in potassium and maintain adequate fluid intake (1,500 mL per day, unless contraindicated).</li>
<li>If GI upset occurs, clients should take the medication with or after meals. ●</li>
<li>Alternate-day dosing can decrease electrolyte imbalance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>c)Potassium-Sparing Diuretics</p>
<p>spironolactone (Aldactone)</p>
<p>Other Medications: triamterene (Dyrenium), amiloride (Midamor)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>Potassium-sparing diuretics block the action of aldosterone (sodium and water retention), which results in potassium retention and the secretion of sodium and water.</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Potassium-sparing diuretics are combined with other diuretics for potassium-sparing effects.</li>
<li>Potassium-sparing diuretics are used for heart failure.</li>
<li>In primary hyperaldosteronism, potassium-sparing diuretics block actions of aldosterone.</li>
<li>Route of administration: Oral</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects;</p>
<ul>
<li>Hyperkalemia (K+ greater than 5.0 mEq/L)</li>
<li>Endocrine effects (impotence in male clients; irregularities of menstrual cycle in female clients)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Contraindications/Precaution</p>
<ul>
<li>Do not administer to clients who have hyperkalemia.</li>
<li>Potassium-sparing diuretics are contraindicated in clients who have severe renal failure and anuria.</li>
</ul>
<p>Medication/Food Interaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Concurrent use of ACE inhibitors increases the risk of hyperkalemia</li>
<li>Concurrent use of potassium supplements increases the risk of hyperkalemia</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain the client’s baseline data.</li>
<li>Monitor the client’s potassium levels regularly.</li>
<li>Can only be given orally.</li>
<li>Teach clients to avoid salt substitutes that contain potassium.</li>
<li>Teach clients to self-monitor blood pressure.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to keep a log of blood pressure and weight.</li>
<li>Warn clients that triamterene may turn urine a bluish color.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="d-osmotic-diuretics">d)Osmotic Diuretics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-osmotic-diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>mannitol (Osmitrol)</li>
<li>Expected Pharmacological Action</li>
<li>Osmotic diuretics reduce intracranial pressure and intraocular pressure by raising serum osmolality and drawing fluid back into the vascular and extravascular space.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Osmotic diuretics prevent renal failure in specific situations, such as hypovolemic shock and severe hypotension.</li>
<li>These medications decrease intracranial pressure (ICP) caused by cerebral edema.</li>
<li>These medications decrease intraocular pressure (IOP).</li>
<li>Osmotic diuretics promote sodium retention and water excretion in clients with hyponatremia and fluid volume excess</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-adverse-effects">Side/Adverse Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-adverse-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Renal failure</li>
<li>Heart failure, pulmonary edema</li>
<li>Fluid and electrolyte imbalances</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>Use extreme caution in clients with heart failure.</li>
</ul>
<p>Interactions</p>
<ul>
<li>Furosemide contributes to therapeutic effect by promoting renal excretion of fluid drawn into vasculature by osmotic diuretics.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Administer mannitol by continuous IV infusion.</li>
<li>To prevent administering microscopic crystals, use a filter needle when drawing from the vial and a filter in the IV tubing.</li>
<li>Monitor daily weight, I &amp; 0, and serum electrolytes.</li>
<li>Monitor for signs of dehydration, acute renal failure, and edema.</li>
<li>Use of furosemide may help prevent rebound fluid retention; this contributes to therapeutic effect.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Carbonic anhydrase inhibitors</p>
<ul>
<li>Blockage of carbonic anhydrase activity induces a sodium bicarbonate diuresis, which reduces body bicarbonate levels.</li>
<li>These drugs include;</li>
<li>Acetazolamide (DIAMOX)</li>
<li>Dichlorphenamide (DARANIDE)</li>
<li>Methazolamide (GLAUCTABS)</li>
</ul>
<p>Acetazolamide administration causes a reduction in aqueous humour and CSF fluid production</p>
<p>acetazolamide cont.’</p>
<ul>
<li>the proximal tubule is the major site of action of carbonic anhydrase inhibitors.</li>
<li>the collecting duct is the secondary site of action .</li>
</ul>
<p>Clinical application</p>
<p>Glaucoma; because acetazolamide decreases the rate of aqueous humor production, a decline in IOP occurs.</p>
<p>The major indication of carbonate anhydrase inhibitor is open angle glaucoma.</p>
<p>It may also be given in secondary glaucoma</p>
<p>Preoperatively in acute angle glaucoma.</p>
<p>Treatment of epilepsy.</p>
<p>Altitude sickness familial periodic paralysis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="toxicity">toxicity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hyper chloremic acidosis.</li>
<li>Renal potassium loss.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindication
Hepatic cirrhosis.</p>
<p>antihypertensive drugs, potential drug targets;</p>
<ul>
<li>CNS: decrease sympathetic tone</li>
<li>Heart: decrease cardiac out put</li>
<li>Veins: dilate; decrease preload</li>
<li>arterioles: dilate; decrease preload</li>
<li>Kidneys: increase diuresis; inhibit renin angiotensin aldosterone</li>
</ul>
<p>Classification of anti hypertensives</p>
<p>• Diuretics:</p>
<p>✓Thiazide and related agents (hydrochlorothiazide, chlorthalidone)</p>
<p>✓Loop diuretics (furosemide, bumetanide,, torsemide, ethacrynic)</p>
<p>✓Potassium sparing diuretics (amiloride, triamterene, spironolactone)</p>
<p>• Angiotensin-converting enzyme (ACE) inhibitors ( captopril, enalapril, lisinopril, quinapril, Ramipril, benazepril)</p>
<p>• Angiotensin II receptor blockers (ARBS)</p>
<p>(losartan, candesartan, Irbesartan, valsartan, telmisartan, eprosartan)</p>
<p>• Calcium channel blockers (CCB)</p>
<p>(verapamil, diltiazem, nifedipine, felodipine, nicardipine, isradipine, amlodipine)</p>
<p>Cont’</p>
<p>Vasodilators</p>
<p>✓Arterial ( hydralazine, minoxidil, diazoxide fenoldopam)</p>
<p>✓Arterial and venous (nitroprusside)</p>
<p>Sympatholytic drugs</p>
<p>Alpha adrenergic blockers; (prazosin, terazosin, doxazosin, phentolamine, phenoxybenzamine)</p>
<p>Beta adrenergic blockers; (metoprolol, atenolol, etc )</p>
<p>Mixed adrenergic; ( labetalol, carvedilol)</p>
<p>Centrally acting alpha2 agonists (methyldopa, clonidine, guanabenz)</p>
<p>Adrenergic neuron blocking agents;( guanethidine, reserpine)</p>
<p>Angiotensin-Converting Enzyme (ACE) Inhibitors</p>
<p>captopril (Capoten)</p>
<p>• Other Medications: Enalapril (Vasotec), Enalaprilat (Vasotec IV), Fosinopril (Monopril), Lisinopril (Prinivil), Ramipril (Altace)</p>
<p>Mechanism of action</p>
<p>ACEIs prevents conversion of angiotensin I to angiotensin II which is a potent vasoconstrictor. this causes vasodilation, reduces peripheral resistance, and decreases secretion of aldosterone (thereby resulting in decrease sodium and water retention and extracellular volume)</p>
<p>Merits of ACEIs</p>
<ul>
<li>Safe for asthmatics, diabetics</li>
<li>Absence of rebound hypertension upon abrupt withdrawal.</li>
<li>Total absence of postural hypotension.</li>
<li>maintains renal blood flow.</li>
<li>devoid of electrolyte imbalance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Therapeutic Uses</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Heart failure</li>
<li>Myocardial infarction (To decrease mortality and to decrease risk of heart failure and left ventricular dysfunction)</li>
<li>Diabetic and nondiabetic nephropathy</li>
<li>For clients at high risk for a cardiovascular event, Ramipril can be used to prevent MI, stroke, or death.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Cough related to inhibition of kinase II (alternative name for ACE) which results in increase in bradykinin</li>
<li>First-dose orthostatic hypotension.</li>
<li>Hyperkalemia</li>
</ul>
<p>Rash and dysgeusia (altered taste), primarily with captopril</p>
<ul>
<li>Angioedema.</li>
<li>Neutropenia (rare but serious complication of captopril)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>These medications are Pregnancy Risk Category D during the second and third trimester, related to fetal injury.</li>
<li>renal stenosis when present bilaterally or in a single remaining kidney.</li>
<li>history of angioedema following use of ACE inhibitor.</li>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with renal impairment and</li>
<li>collagen vascular disease because they are at greater risk for developing neutropenia. Closely monitor these clients for signs of infection.</li>
<li>hypotension</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medication-food-interactions">Medication/Food Interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medication-food-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diuretics can contribute to first-dose hypotension</li>
<li>Antihypertensive medications may have an additive hypotensive effect.</li>
<li>Potassium supplements and potassium-sparing diuretics increase the risk of hyperkalemia.</li>
<li>ACE inhibitors can increase levels of lithium carbonate (Eskalith)</li>
<li>Use of NSAIDs may decrease the antihypertensive effect of ACE inhibitors.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Administer ACE inhibitors orally except enalapril, which is the only ACE inhibitor for IV use.</li>
<li>Advise clients that the medication may be prescribed as a single formulation or in combination with hydrochlorothiazide.</li>
<li>Advise clients that blood pressure has to be monitored after the first dose for at least 2 hr. to detect hypotension.</li>
<li>Instruct clients that captopril should be taken at least 1 hr. before meals. All other ACE inhibitors can be taken with or without food.</li>
<li>Advise clients to notify the provider if cough, rash, dysgeusia (lack of taste), and/or signs of infection occur</li>
</ul>
<p>Angiotensin II Receptor Blockers (ARBs)</p>
<p>• losartan (Cozaar)</p>
<p>• Other Medications: Valsartan (Diovan) , Irbesartan (Avapro) , Candesartan (Atacand) , Olmesartan (Benicar)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>These medications block the action of angiotensin II in the body.</p>
<p>This results in:</p>
<p>• Vasodilation (mostly arteriole)</p>
<p>• Excretion of sodium and water, and retention of potassium (through effects on the kidney)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypertension,</li>
<li>Heart failure and prevention of mortality following MI,</li>
<li>Stroke prevention ,</li>
<li>Delay progression of diabetic nephropathy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The major difference between ARBs and ACE inhibitors is that cough and hyperkalemia are not side effects of ARBs</p>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<p>• Angioedema</p>
<p>contraindication</p>
<p>• Hypersensitivity</p>
<p>• Pregnancy</p>
<p>• renal stenosis when present bilaterally or in a single remaining kidney</p>
<p>considerations</p>
<p>monitor BP, HR, Weight, Edema, Blood Urea Nitrogen, Serum Creatinine.</p>
<p>Can be used in patients intolerant to ACEI’s (due to cough)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="calcium-channel-blockers">CALCIUM CHANNEL BLOCKERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calcium-channel-blockers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nifedipine (Adalat, Procardia)</li>
<li>Verapamil (Calan)</li>
<li>Amlodipine (Norvasc)</li>
</ul>
<p>Other Medications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Amlodipine (Norvasc)</li>
<li>Felodipine (Plendil)</li>
<li>Nicardipine (Cardene, Cleviprex)</li>
<li>Diltiazem (Cardizem)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action of CCB</p>
<p>• inhibits calcium influx in the smooth muscles and the myocardium.</p>
<p>• Blocking of calcium channels in blood vessels leads to vasodilation of peripheral arterioles and arteries/arterioles of the heart, slows down heart conduction and reduction of blood pressure.</p>
<p>NIFEDIPINE (ADALAT)</p>
<p>• give rise to coronary vasodilation.</p>
<p>• Enhances coronary blood flow.</p>
<p>• Reduces total periphery resistance, reduces systolic and diastolic pressure</p>
<p>Therapeutic use</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic angina</li>
<li>Congestive heart failure</li>
<li>Acute myocardial infarction</li>
<li>Peripheral vascular disorders</li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse drug reaction</p>
<p>Palpitation, nausea, vomiting, flushing, headache, edema.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="amlodipine">amlodipine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amlodipine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Serves as a long acting calcium channel blocker.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic use</p>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of essential hypertension.</li>
<li>Angina pectoris</li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse drug reaction
Palpitation,epixtasis,cough,nocturia,musclecramps,breathless,importen ce, conjunctivitis</p>
<p>verapamil</p>
<ul>
<li>Enhances coronary blood flow rate,vasodilation.</li>
<li>Exerts anti arrhythmic action.</li>
<li>Reduces peripheral resistance.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Supraventricular tachycardia.</li>
<li>Acute coronary spasms</li>
<li>Angina pectoris</li>
<li>Hypertension with myocardial infarction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Adverse reaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Dizziness</li>
<li>Vertigo</li>
<li>Constipation</li>
<li>Hypotension</li>
<li>Nausea</li>
<li>Pedal edema</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing considerations</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor BP, HR, rhythm,</li>
<li>Control calcium supplement.</li>
<li>Inform patient not to stop drug abruptly.</li>
<li>Patient to report signs of adverse effects such as irregular heart beat, shortness of breath, oedema in the hands and feet, dizziness, constipation, nausea and hypotension.</li>
<li>Discontinue in breast feeding because they are excreted in breast milk and have potential for adverse effects in neonates.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="direct-acting-vasodilators">DIRECT ACTING VASODILATORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-acting-vasodilators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hydralazine">HYDRALAZINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hydralazine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hydralazine (APRESOLINE) causes direct relaxation of the arterio smooth muscle secondary to a fall in the intracellular calcium. this is associated with powerful stimulation of the sympathetic nervous system, due to baroreceptor mediated reflexes</p>
<p>Toxicity and precaution</p>
<ul>
<li>These includes; headache, nausea, flushing, hypotension, palpitation, tachycardia, dizziness and angina pectoris.</li>
<li>Myocardial ischemia (increased oxygen demand)</li>
<li>Immunological reactions, drug induced lupus syndrome. this occurs after six months of treatment with hydralazine.</li>
<li>symptoms include, arthralgia, arthritis and fever.</li>
<li>The treatment can result in an illness that resembles serum sickness, hemolytic anaemia, vasculitis, and glomerulonephritis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Therapeutic uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Due to adverse effect profile, hydralazine is no longer a first line drug in the treatment of hypertension.</li>
<li>Used in patients with CCF(in combination with nitrates for patients who cannot tolerate ACE inhibitors.</li>
<li>Treatment of hypertension emergencies in pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>(especially preeclampsia).</p>
<p>The usual dose is twenty five to 100mgs twice a day</p>
<p>The maximum recommended dose of hydralazine is 200mg/day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindication">Contraindication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Parenteral administration in coronary artery disease.</li>
<li>Elderly patients</li>
</ul>
<p>ALPHA ADRENERGIC BLOCKERS (SYMPATHOLYTICS)</p>
<ul>
<li>Medication: prazosin (Minipress)</li>
<li>doxazosin mesylate (Cardura)</li>
</ul>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>It inhibits Alpha adrenergic receptor causing Venous and arterial dilation leading to reduction in total peripheral vascular resistance.</li>
<li>Smooth muscle relaxation of the prostatic capsule and bladder neck</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Primary hypertension.</li>
<li>Doxazosin mesylate (Cardura) may be used to decrease symptoms of benign prostatic hypertrophy (BPH), which include urgency, frequency, and dysuria.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">Cont'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Side/Adverse Effects</li>
<li>First-dose orthostatic hypotension</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>• Pregnancy</p>
<p>• Clients with hypersensitivity to medication</p>
<p>• Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>• NSAIDs and clonidine may decrease the antihypertensive effects of prazosin.</p>
<p>• Advise clients to avoid OTC NSAIDs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-administration">Nursing Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Obtain baseline blood pressure and heart rate.</li>
<li>Instruct clients that the medication can be taken with food.</li>
<li>Recommend that clients take the initial dose at bedtime to decrease "first-dose" hypotensive effect.</li>
<li>Start treatment with low dosage of medication.</li>
<li>First dose may be given at night.</li>
<li>Monitor blood pressure for 2 hr . after the initiation of treatment.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to avoid activities requiring mental alertness for the first 12 to 24 hr .</li>
<li>Instruct clients to change positions slowly and to lie down if feeling dizzy, lightheaded, or faint</li>
<li>Antihypertensive medications may have an additive hypotensive effect, instruct clients to observe for signs of hypotension (dizziness, lightheadedness, faintness).</li>
</ul>
<p>CENTRALLY ACTING ALPHA2 AGONISTS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clonidine-catapres">clonidine (Catapres)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clonidine-catapres" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>guanfacine HCl (Tenex),</li>
<li>methyldopa (Aldomet)</li>
</ul>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>These medications act within the CNS to decrease sympathetic outflow resulting in decreased stimulation of the adrenergic receptors (both alpha and beta receptors) of the heart and peripheral vascular system.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decrease in sympathetic outflow to the myocardium results in bradycardia and decreased cardiac output (CO).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decrease in sympathetic outflow to the peripheral vasculature results in vasodilation, which leads to decreased blood pressure.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Primary hypertension (administered alone, with a diuretic, or with another antihypertensive agent)</li>
<li>Severe cancer pain (administered parenterally by epidural infusion)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigational-use">Investigational use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigational-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Migraine headache</li>
<li>Flushing from menopause</li>
<li>Management of ADHD and Tourette's syndrome</li>
<li>Management of withdrawal symptoms from alcohol, tobacco, and opioids</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<p>• Drowsiness and sedation</p>
<p>• Dry mouth</p>
<p>• Rebound hypertension</p>
<p>contraindication</p>
<p>• Clonidine is Pregnancy Risk Category C.</p>
<p>• Avoid use during lactation.</p>
<p>• This medication is contraindicated for clients taking anticoagulant medications</p>
<p>• Avoid use of transdermal patch on affected skin in scleroderma and systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE).</p>
<p>• Use cautiously in clients with cerebrovascular disease, recent MI, diabetes mellitus, major depressive disorder, or chronic renal failure</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Antihypertensive medications may have an additive hypotensive effect.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Concurrent use of prazosin (Minipress), MAOI s, and tricyclic antidepressants can counteract the antihypertensive effect of clonidine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Additive CNS depression can occur with concurrent use of other CNS depressants, such as alcohol.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-administration">Nursing Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Administer medication by oral, epidural, and transdermal routes.</li>
<li>Medication is usually administered twice a day in divided doses. Take larger dose at bedtime to decrease the occurrence of daytime sleepiness.</li>
<li>Transdermal patches are applied every seven days. Advise clients to apply patch on hairless, intact skin on torso or upper arm.</li>
</ul>
<p>Methyldopa (ALDOMET)</p>
<ul>
<li>Acts through its metabolites (methylnorepinephrine)which stimulates central alpha adrenergic receptors, thus reducing total peripheral resistance.</li>
<li>It does not affect glomerular filtration, cardiac output or heart rate.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic effects</p>
<p>moderate to severe hypertension</p>
<p>Adverse effects:</p>
<p>GIT upsets, sedation, depression, nasal stuffiness, myocarditis edema, orthostatic hypotension, diarrhea, dry mouth, erectile dysfunction, eosinophilia, hemolytic anemia, fever.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>contraindication</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity, activity liver disease, those who developed liver cirrhosis with previous treatment of methyldopa.</li>
</ul>
<p>Caution;</p>
<ul>
<li>Patients taking diuretics and antihypertensive.</li>
<li>Those taking levodopa because of potential for additive antihypertensive effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>Consideration</p>
<ul>
<li>patient to avoid hazardous task.</li>
<li>Lower dose in impaired renal disease.</li>
<li>Monitor liver functions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Caution cont.'</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor HB, RBCs for signs of anemia.</li>
<li>Monitor weight, fluid input and out put.</li>
<li>Signs of drug induced depression,</li>
<li>Take BP in different patients position during dose adjustments, warn of signs and symptoms of adverse effects and toxicity</li>
<li>Tolerance may develop 2to 3 weeks after start of treatment.</li>
<li>Urine may darken on exposure to air(as drug is broken down to its metabolites)</li>
<li>Dose increase should be made with the evening dose to minimize the effects of drowsiness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>BETA ADRENERGIC BLOCKERS (SYMPATHOLYTICS)</p>
<p>Cardioselective: Beta1</p>
<p>• Metoprolol (Lopressor)</p>
<p>• Atenolol (Tenormin)</p>
<p>• Metoprolol succinate (Toprol XL)</p>
<p>• Esmolol HCL (Brevibloc)</p>
<p>Nonselective: (Beta1 and Beta2)</p>
<p>• Propranolol (Inderal)</p>
<p>• Nadolol (Corgard)</p>
<p>• Labetalol (Normodyne)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>They block beta- adrenergic receptors in the myocardium and in the electrical conduction system of the heart.</p>
<p>• Decreased heart rate</p>
<p>• Decreased myocardial contractility</p>
<p>• Decreased rate of conduction through the AV node</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>hypertension , Angina, arrhythmias, heart failure and myocardial infarction.</p>
<p>Other uses may include: Treatment of hyperthyroidism, migraine headache, pheochromocytoma, and glaucoma</p>
<p>adverse effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Bradycardia, fatigue, dizziness, nightmares, depression, memory loss, hallucination, impotence, cold extremities, elevated serum cholesterol.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindication</p>
<p>severe hypotension, bradycardia, congestive heart failure, asthma, diabetics, critically abnormal lipid profile</p>
<p>Consideration</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the rationale of therapy and importance of taking drugs as prescribed.</li>
<li>Patient should not discontinue drugs abruptly because it can cause MI or angina</li>
</ul>
<p>Consideration cont.'</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise clients to avoid sudden changes in position to prevent occurrence of orthostatic hypotension</li>
<li>Administer medications orally, usually once or twice a day.</li>
<li>Administer the following medications by IV route: atenolol, metoprolol, labetalol, propranolol.</li>
<li>Teach clients to self monitor heart rate and blood pressure at home on a daily basis.</li>
<li>Monitor weight &amp; signs of hypovolemic shock especially in diabetic patients.</li>
<li>Glucagon is prescribed to reverse signs of overdose.</li>
<li>Dose are lowered in geriatrics due to delayed metabolism and enhanced side effects.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Medications for Hypertensive Crisis</p>
<p>nitroprusside sodium (Nitropress)</p>
<p>Other Medications:</p>
<p>Nitroglycerin (Nitrostat IV)</p>
<p>Nicardipine (Cardene)</p>
<p>Clevidipine (Cleviprex)</p>
<p>Enalaprilat (Vasotec IV)</p>
<p>Esmolol HCL (Brevibloc)</p>
<p>mechanism of Action Direct vasodilation of arteries and veins resulting in rapid reduction of blood pressure (decreased preload and afterload) ● Therapeutic Uses Hypertensive emergencies</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects">Side effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Excessive hypotension</p>
<ul>
<li>Administer medication slowly because rapid administration will cause blood pressure to go down rapidly.</li>
<li>Monitor the client's blood pressure and ECG.</li>
</ul>
<p>Interactions</p>
<p>Nitroprusside should not be administered in the same infusion as any other medication.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>• Prepare medication by adding to diluent for IV infusion.</p>
<p>• Note color of solution. Solution may be light brown in color. Discard solution of any other color.</p>
<p>• Protect IV container and tubing from light.</p>
<p>• Discard medication after 24 hr.</p>
<p>• Monitor vital signs and ECG continuously</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cardiac-glycoside">CARDIAC GLYCOSIDE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cardiac-glycoside" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Two main types</p>
<ul>
<li>cardenolides (digitalis, convallaria, oleandra)</li>
<li>Bufadienolides (Helleborus, Poison Arrow Frog)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action
Cardiac glycoside slows down the heart rate and increase the force of contraction</p>
<p>Pharmacological action</p>
<ul>
<li>Enhances myocardial contractility and is used in congestive cardiac failure.</li>
<li>Enhances cardiac output, minimizes dilated cardiac size, blood volume and venous pressure.</li>
<li>They modulate autonomic nervous system activity, and this contributes to their efficacy in management of heart failure.</li>
<li>Diuretic effect, reduce oedema.</li>
<li>It is usually given only when diuretics and ACEIs have failed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indication">Indication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Congestive heart failure, heart failure with atrial fibrillation, or pts who remain symptomatic despite therapy with ACE inhibitors and b Adrenergic receptor antagonists</li>
<li>Left ventricular failure.</li>
<li>Atrial fibrillation.</li>
</ul>
<p>digoxin</p>
<ul>
<li>It is the most commonly used digitalis</li>
</ul>
<p>forms</p>
<p>Tablets (Lanoxin)</p>
<p>Capsules (lanoxicaps)</p>
<p>Parenteral digoxin is available for intravenous administration and maintenance doses can be given intravenously when oral dosing is impractical.</p>
<p>Digoxin cont.’</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>Positive inotropic effect</p>
<p>✓ increased force of myocardial contraction Increased force and efficiency of myocardial contraction improves the heart's effectiveness as a pump,</p>
<p>✓ improving stroke volume and cardiac output.</p>
<p>✓ Increase perfusion of the kidneys which facilitates excretion of fluid by the kidneys</p>
<p>Negative chronotropic effect</p>
<p>✓ decreased heart rate ,</p>
<p>✓ At therapeutic levels, digoxin slows the rate of SA node depolarization and the rate of impulses through the conduction system of the heart.</p>
<p>✓ A decreased heart rate gives the ventricles more time to fill with blood coming from the atria, which leads to increased SV and increased CO.</p>
<p>Digoxin cont.’</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>• Treatment of heart failure</p>
<p>• Dysrhythmias (atrial fibrillation)</p>
<p>side/adverse effects</p>
<p>• Dysrhythmias (caused by interfering with the electrical conduction in the myocardium)</p>
<p>• Cardiotoxicity leading to bradycardia.</p>
<p>• GI effects include anorexia (usually the first sign), nausea, vomiting, and abdominal pain.</p>
<p>• Teach clients to monitor for these effects and report to the provider if they occur.</p>
<p>• CNS effects include fatigue, weakness, vision changes (diplopia, blurred vision, yellow-green or white halos around objects).</p>
<p>Digoxin cont.’</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>• In Pregnancy</p>
<p>• clients with disturbances in ventricular rhythm, including ventricular fibrillation, ventricular tachycardia, and second- and third-degree heart block.</p>
<p>• Use cautiously in clients who have hypokalemia, partial AV block, advanced heart failure, and renal insufficiency.</p>
<p>Medication interaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Thiazide diuretics, such as hydrochlorothiazide (HCTZ), and loop diuretics, such as furosemide (Lasix), may lead to hypokalemia, which increases the risk of developing dysrhythmias</li>
<li>ACE inhibitors and ARBs increase the risk of hyperkalemia, which can lead to decreased therapeutic effects of digoxin.</li>
<li>Sympathomimetic medications such as dopamine (Intropin) complement the inotropic action of digoxin and increase the rate and force of heart muscle contraction.</li>
<li>Quinidine increases the risk of digoxin toxicity when used concurrently.</li>
<li>Verapamil (Calan) increases plasma levels</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drugs-used-in-coagulation-disorders">Drugs used in Coagulation Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-used-in-coagulation-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="by-geoffrey">By Geoffrey<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#by-geoffrey" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a6970a92"><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>11</mn><mtext>th&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">11^{\text {th }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> November 2024<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a6970a92" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hemostasis is important in clot formation to prevent blood loss.</li>
<li>However, there can be situations in the body there is formation of unwanted clot (thrombus) within the blood vessels. This is called hypercoagulable state.</li>
<li>Conditions like atherosclerosis, bedridden for long time and major surgeries can lead to hypercoagulable state (clot formation).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Also, blood may fail to form a clot in disorders like haemophilia A, deficiency of vitamin K which may warrant platelet transfusion or supplement of vitamin-K.</li>
<li>Rudolph Virchow defined three predisposing factors leading to abnormal clot formation within the blood vessels (commonly known as Virchow's triad)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The Virchow's triad consists of; vessel wall injury, altered blood flow and hypercoagulability state.</li>
<li>Drugs acting on hemostasis can act at one of the following points;
» Blood coagulation (fibrin formation)
» Platelet function
» Fibrin removal (fibrinolysis)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="embolus-vs-thrombus">Embolus Vs. Thrombus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#embolus-vs-thrombus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Thrombus- a clot that is adherent to the wall of the blood vessel</li>
<li>Embolus- a clot floating on blood and can be carried away causing blockage of blood flow.</li>
<li>A thrombus can detached from the wall of the blood vessel hence becomes an emboli</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="coagulation-cascade">Coagulation Cascade<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coagulation-cascade" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Coagulation is conversion of liquid blood to a clot.</li>
<li>The end results is conversion of soluble fibrinogen to insoluble strands of fibrin.</li>
<li>Blood clotting factors are inactive in blood but when the are activated they are designated by the suffix "a" e.g. VIIa, Xa, Xia, thrombin (IIa) etc.</li>
<li>When one factor is activated, it catalyses the formation of another factor in larger amount and so on.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="coagulation-cascade">Coagulation Cascade<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coagulation-cascade" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Vascular endothelium and antithrombin III are the inhibitors of cascade formation.</li>
<li>There are two pathways of coagulation cascade; intrinsic pathway and extrinsic pathway.</li>
<li>Intrinsic pathway occurs in the blood vessels while extrinsic occurs when the tissue is injured and is initiated by the tissue factor (prothrombin)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-role-of-thrombin">The role of thrombin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-role-of-thrombin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Thrombin (factor IIa) cleaves fibrinogen to form fibrin.</li>
<li>Activates factor XIIIa a fibrinoligase which strengthens fibrin to fibrin linkages.</li>
<li>It activates platelet aggregation.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="table-48-1-some-substances-that-promote-or-inhibit-haemostasis">Table 48.1 Some substances that promote or inhibit haemostasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#table-48-1-some-substances-that-promote-or-inhibit-haemostasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="promoters-of-coagulation">PROMOTERS OF COAGULATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#promoters-of-coagulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Adenosine diphosphate (ADP)
Plasminogen activator inhibitor
Thromboplastin
Thromboxane A,
von Willebrand factor</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inhibitors-of-coagulation">INHIBITORS OF COAGULATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inhibitors-of-coagulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Activated protein C
cAMP
Nitric oxide
Prostacyclin
Thrombomodulin
Tissue plasminogen activator (t-PA)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="coagulation-defects">Coagulation Defects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coagulation-defects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Deficiency of coagulation factors i.e haemophilia A (deficiency of factor VIII) and hemophilia B (lack of factor IX, chrismas factor)</li>
<li>Acquired clotting defects- liver disease, vitamin K deficiency, excessive anticoagulant therapy</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drugs-used-in-coagulation-defects">Drugs used in coagulation Defects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-used-in-coagulation-defects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
